Both are pushed onto the mark stack.\\n56: class G1TaskQueueEntry {\\n57: private:\\n58:   void* _holder;\\n59: \\n60:   static const uintptr_t ArraySliceBit = 1;\\n61: \\n62:   G1TaskQueueEntry(oop obj) : _holder(obj) {\\n63:     assert(_holder != nullptr, \\\"Not allowed to set null task queue element\\\");\\n64:   }\\n65:   G1TaskQueueEntry(HeapWord* addr) : _holder((void*)((uintptr_t)addr | ArraySliceBit)) { }\\n66: public:\\n67: \\n68:   G1TaskQueueEntry() : _holder(nullptr) { }\\n69:   // Trivially copyable, for use in GenericTaskQueue.\\n70: \\n71:   static G1TaskQueueEntry from_slice(HeapWord* what) { return G1TaskQueueEntry(what); }\\n72:   static G1TaskQueueEntry from_oop(oop obj) { return G1TaskQueueEntry(obj); }\\n73: \\n74:   oop obj() const {\\n75:     assert(!is_array_slice(), \\\"Trying to read array slice \\\" PTR_FORMAT \\\" as oop\\\", p2i(_holder));\\n76:     return cast_to_oop(_holder);\\n77:   }\\n78: \\n79:   HeapWord* slice() const {\\n80:     assert(is_array_slice(), \\\"Trying to read oop \\\" PTR_FORMAT \\\" as array slice\\\", p2i(_holder));\\n81:     return (HeapWord*)((uintptr_t)_holder & ~ArraySliceBit);\\n82:   }\\n83: \\n84:   bool is_oop() const { return !is_array_slice(); }\\n85:   bool is_array_slice() const { return ((uintptr_t)_holder & ArraySliceBit) != 0; }\\n86:   bool is_null() const { return _holder == nullptr; }\\n87: };\\n88: \\n89: typedef GenericTaskQueue<G1TaskQueueEntry, mtGC> G1CMTaskQueue;\\n90: typedef GenericTaskQueueSet<G1CMTaskQueue, mtGC> G1CMTaskQueueSet;\\n91: \\n92: // Closure used by CM during concurrent reference discovery\\n93: // and reference processing (during remarking) to determine\\n94: // if a particular object is alive. It is primarily used\\n95: // to determine if referents of discovered reference objects\\n96: // are alive. An instance is also embedded into the\\n97: // reference processor as the _is_alive_non_header field\\n98: class G1CMIsAliveClosure : public BoolObjectClosure {\\n99:   G1ConcurrentMark* _cm;\\n100: \\n101: public:\\n102:   G1CMIsAliveClosure();\\n103:   G1CMIsAliveClosure(G1ConcurrentMark* cm);\\n104:   void initialize(G1ConcurrentMark* cm);\\n105: \\n106:   bool do_object_b(oop obj);\\n107: };\\n108: \\n109: class G1CMSubjectToDiscoveryClosure : public BoolObjectClosure {\\n110:   G1CollectedHeap* _g1h;\\n111: public:\\n112:   G1CMSubjectToDiscoveryClosure(G1CollectedHeap* g1h) : _g1h(g1h) { }\\n113:   bool do_object_b(oop obj);\\n114: };\\n115: \\n116: // Represents the overflow mark stack used by concurrent marking.\\n117: //\\n118: // Stores oops in a huge buffer in virtual memory that is always fully committed.\\n119: // Resizing may only happen during a STW pause when the stack is empty.\\n120: //\\n121: // Memory is allocated on a \\\"chunk\\\" basis, i.e. a set of oops. For this, the mark\\n122: // stack memory is split into evenly sized chunks of oops. Users can only\\n123: // add or remove entries on that basis.\\n124: // Chunks are filled in increasing address order. Not completely filled chunks\\n125: // have a null element as a terminating element.\\n126: //\\n127: // Every chunk has a header containing a single pointer element used for memory\\n128: // management. This wastes some space, but is negligible (< .1% with current sizing).\\n129: //\\n130: // Memory management is done using a mix of tracking a high water-mark indicating\\n131: // that all chunks at a lower address are valid chunks, and a singly linked free\\n132: // list connecting all empty chunks.\\n133: class G1CMMarkStack {\\n134: public:\\n135:   // Number of TaskQueueEntries that can fit in a single chunk.\\n136:   static const size_t EntriesPerChunk = 1024 - 1 /* One reference for the next pointer */;\\n137: private:\\n138:   struct TaskQueueEntryChunk {\\n139:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* next;\\n140:     G1TaskQueueEntry data[EntriesPerChunk];\\n141:   };\\n142: \\n143:   class ChunkAllocator {\\n144:     // The chunk allocator relies on a growable array data structure that allows resizing without the\\n145:     // need to copy existing items. The basic approach involves organizing the array into chunks,\\n146:     // essentially creating an \\\"array of arrays\\\"; referred to as buckets in this implementation. To\\n147:     // facilitate efficient indexing, the size of the first bucket is set to a power of 2. This choice\\n148:     // allows for quick conversion of an array index into a bucket index and the corresponding offset\\n149:     // within the bucket. Additionally, each new bucket added to the growable array doubles the capacity of\\n150:     // the growable array.\\n151:     //\\n152:     // Illustration of the growable array data structure.\\n153:     //\\n154:     //        +----+        +----+----+\\n155:     //        |    |------->|    |    |\\n156:     //        |    |        +----+----+\\n157:     //        +----+        +----+----+\\n158:     //        |    |------->|    |    |\\n159:     //        |    |        +----+----+\\n160:     //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\\n161:     //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |\\n162:     //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\\n163:     //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\\n164:     //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |     |     |     |    |\\n165:     //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\\n166:     //        +----+\\n167:     //\\n168:     size_t _min_capacity;\\n169:     size_t _max_capacity;\\n170:     size_t _capacity;\\n171:     size_t _num_buckets;\\n172:     bool _should_grow;\\n173:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* _buckets;\\n174:     char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\\n175:     volatile size_t _size;\\n176:     char _pad4[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(size_t)];\\n177: \\n178:     size_t bucket_size(size_t bucket) {\\n179:       return (bucket == 0) ?\\n180:               _min_capacity :\\n181:               _min_capacity * ( 1ULL << (bucket - 1));\\n182:     }\\n183: \\n184:     static unsigned int find_highest_bit(uintptr_t mask) {\\n185:       return count_leading_zeros(mask) ^ (BitsPerWord - 1U);\\n186:     }\\n187: \\n188:     size_t get_bucket(size_t array_idx) {\\n189:       if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\\n190:         return 0;\\n191:       }\\n192: \\n193:       return find_highest_bit(array_idx) - find_highest_bit(_min_capacity) + 1;\\n194:     }\\n195: \\n196:     size_t get_bucket_index(size_t array_idx) {\\n197:       if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\\n198:         return array_idx;\\n199:       }\\n200:       return array_idx - (1ULL << find_highest_bit(array_idx));\\n201:     }\\n202: \\n203:     bool reserve(size_t new_capacity);\\n204: \\n205:   public:\\n206:     ChunkAllocator();\\n207: \\n208:     ~ChunkAllocator();\\n209: \\n210:     bool initialize(size_t initial_capacity, size_t max_capacity);\\n211: \\n212:     void reset() {\\n213:       _size = 0;\\n214:       _should_grow = false;\\n215:     }\\n216: \\n217:     // During G1CMConcurrentMarkingTask or finalize_marking phases, we prefer to restart the marking when\\n218:     // the G1CMMarkStack overflows. Attempts to expand the G1CMMarkStack should be followed with a restart\\n219:     // of the marking. On failure to allocate a new chuck, the caller just returns and forces a restart.\\n220:     // This approach offers better memory utilization for the G1CMMarkStack, as each iteration of the\\n221:     // marking potentially involves traversing fewer unmarked nodes in the graph.\\n222: \\n223:     // However, during the reference processing phase, instead of restarting the marking process, the\\n224:     // G1CMMarkStack is expanded upon failure to allocate a new chunk. The decision between these two\\n225:     // modes of expansion is determined by the _should_grow parameter.\\n226:     void set_should_grow() {\\n227:       _should_grow = true;\\n228:     }\\n229: \\n230:     size_t capacity() const { return _capacity; }\\n231: \\n232:     // Expand the mark stack doubling its size.\\n233:     bool try_expand();\\n234:     bool try_expand_to(size_t desired_capacity);\\n235: \\n236:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* allocate_new_chunk();\\n237:   };\\n238: \\n239:   ChunkAllocator _chunk_allocator;\\n240: \\n241:   char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\\n242:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _free_list;  // Linked list of free chunks that can be allocated by users.\\n243:   char _pad1[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*)];\\n244:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _chunk_list; // List of chunks currently containing data.\\n245:   volatile size_t _chunks_in_chunk_list;\\n246:   char _pad2[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*) - sizeof(size_t)];\\n247: \\n248:   // Atomically add the given chunk to the list.\\n249:   void add_chunk_to_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* list, TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\\n250:   // Atomically remove and return a chunk from the given list. Returns null if the\\n251:   // list is empty.\\n252:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* list);\\n253: \\n254:   void add_chunk_to_chunk_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\\n255:   void add_chunk_to_free_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\\n256: \\n257:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_chunk_list();\\n258:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_free_list();\\n259: \\n260:  public:\\n261:   G1CMMarkStack();\\n262:   ~G1CMMarkStack() = default;\\n263: \\n264:   // Alignment and minimum capacity of this mark stack in number of oops.\\n265:   static size_t capacity_alignment();\\n266: \\n267:   // Allocate and initialize the mark stack.\\n268:   bool initialize();\\n269: \\n270:   // Pushes the given buffer containing at most EntriesPerChunk elements on the mark\\n271:   // stack. If less than EntriesPerChunk elements are to be pushed, the array must\\n272:   // be terminated with a null.\\n273:   // Returns whether the buffer contents were successfully pushed to the global mark\\n274:   // stack.\\n275:   bool par_push_chunk(G1TaskQueueEntry* buffer);\\n276: \\n277:   // Pops a chunk from this mark stack, copying them into the given buffer. This\\n278:   // chunk may contain up to EntriesPerChunk elements. If there are less, the last\\n279:   // element in the array is a null pointer.\\n280:   bool par_pop_chunk(G1TaskQueueEntry* buffer);\\n281: \\n282:   // Return whether the chunk list is empty. Racy due to unsynchronized access to\\n283:   // _chunk_list.\\n284:   bool is_empty() const { return _chunk_list == nullptr; }\\n285: \\n286:   size_t capacity() const  { return _chunk_allocator.capacity(); }\\n287: \\n288:   void set_should_grow() {\\n289:     _chunk_allocator.set_should_grow();\\n290:   }\\n291: \\n292:   // Expand the stack, typically in response to an overflow condition\\n293:   void expand();\\n294: \\n295:   // Return the approximate number of oops on this mark stack. Racy due to\\n296:   // unsynchronized access to _chunks_in_chunk_list.\\n297:   size_t size() const { return _chunks_in_chunk_list * EntriesPerChunk; }\\n298: \\n299:   void set_empty();\\n300: \\n301:   // Apply Fn to every oop on the mark stack. The mark stack must not\\n302:   // be modified while iterating.\\n303:   template<typename Fn> void iterate(Fn fn) const PRODUCT_RETURN;\\n304: };\\n305: \\n306: // Root MemRegions are memory areas that contain objects which references are\\n307: // roots wrt to the marking. They must be scanned before marking to maintain the\\n308: // SATB invariant.\\n309: // Typically they contain the areas from TAMS to top of the regions.\\n310: // We could scan and mark through these objects during the concurrent start pause,\\n311: // but for pause time reasons we move this work to the concurrent phase.\\n312: // We need to complete this procedure before we can evacuate a particular region\\n313: // because evacuation might determine that some of these \\\"root objects\\\" are dead,\\n314: // potentially dropping some required references.\\n315: // Root MemRegions comprise of the contents of survivor regions at the end\\n316: // of the GC, and any objects copied into the old gen during GC.\\n317: class G1CMRootMemRegions {\\n318:   // The set of root MemRegions.\\n319:   MemRegion* _root_regions;\\n320:   size_t const _max_regions;\\n321: \\n322:   volatile size_t _num_root_regions; // Actual number of root regions.\\n323: \\n324:   volatile size_t _claimed_root_regions; // Number of root regions currently claimed.\\n325: \\n326:   volatile bool _scan_in_progress;\\n327:   volatile bool _should_abort;\\n328: \\n329:   void notify_scan_done();\\n330: \\n331: public:\\n332:   G1CMRootMemRegions(uint const max_regions);\\n333:   ~G1CMRootMemRegions();\\n334: \\n335:   // Reset the data structure to allow addition of new root regions.\\n336:   void reset();\\n337: \\n338:   void add(HeapWord* start, HeapWord* end);\\n339: \\n340:   // Reset the claiming / scanning of the root regions.\\n341:   void prepare_for_scan();\\n342: \\n343:   // Forces get_next() to return null so that the iteration aborts early.\\n344:   void abort() { _should_abort = true; }\\n345: \\n346:   // Return true if the CM thread are actively scanning root regions,\\n347:   // false otherwise.\\n348:   bool scan_in_progress() { return _scan_in_progress; }\\n349: \\n350:   // Claim the next root MemRegion to scan atomically, or return null if\\n351:   // all have been claimed.\\n352:   const MemRegion* claim_next();\\n353: \\n354:   // The number of root regions to scan.\\n355:   uint num_root_regions() const;\\n356: \\n357:   // Is the given memregion contained in the root regions; the MemRegion must\\n358:   // match exactly.\\n359:   bool contains(const MemRegion mr) const;\\n360: \\n361:   void cancel_scan();\\n362: \\n363:   // Flag that we're done with root region scanning and notify anyone\\n364:   // who's waiting on it. If aborted is false, assume that all regions\\n365:   // have been claimed.\\n366:   void scan_finished();\\n367: \\n368:   // If CM threads are still scanning root regions, wait until they\\n369:   // are done. Return true if we had to wait, false otherwise.\\n370:   bool wait_until_scan_finished();\\n371: };\\n372: \\n373: // This class manages data structures and methods for doing liveness analysis in\\n374: // G1's concurrent cycle.\\n375: class G1ConcurrentMark : public CHeapObj<mtGC> {\\n376:   friend class G1CMBitMapClosure;\\n377:   friend class G1CMConcurrentMarkingTask;\\n378:   friend class G1CMDrainMarkingStackClosure;\\n379:   friend class G1CMKeepAliveAndDrainClosure;\\n380:   friend class G1CMRefProcProxyTask;\\n381:   friend class G1CMRemarkTask;\\n382:   friend class G1CMRootRegionScanTask;\\n383:   friend class G1CMTask;\\n384:   friend class G1ConcurrentMarkThread;\\n385: \\n386:   G1ConcurrentMarkThread* _cm_thread;     // The thread doing the work\\n387:   G1CollectedHeap*        _g1h;           // The heap\\n388: \\n389:   // Concurrent marking support structures\\n390:   G1CMBitMap              _mark_bitmap;\\n391: \\n392:   // Heap bounds\\n393:   MemRegion const         _heap;\\n394: \\n395:   // Root region tracking and claiming\\n396:   G1CMRootMemRegions      _root_regions;\\n397: \\n398:   // For grey objects\\n399:   G1CMMarkStack           _global_mark_stack; // Grey objects behind global finger\\n400:   HeapWord* volatile      _finger;            // The global finger, region aligned,\\n401:                                               // always pointing to the end of the\\n402:                                               // last claimed region\\n403: \\n404:   uint                    _worker_id_offset;\\n405:   uint                    _max_num_tasks;    // Maximum number of marking tasks\\n406:   uint                    _num_active_tasks; // Number of tasks currently active\\n407:   G1CMTask**              _tasks;            // Task queue array (max_worker_id length)\\n408: \\n409:   G1CMTaskQueueSet*       _task_queues; // Task queue set\\n410:   TaskTerminator          _terminator;  // For termination\\n411: \\n412:   // Two sync barriers that are used to synchronize tasks when an\\n413:   // overflow occurs. The algorithm is the following. All tasks enter\\n414:   // the first one to ensure that they have all stopped manipulating\\n415:   // the global data structures. After they exit it, they re-initialize\\n416:   // their data structures and task 0 re-initializes the global data\\n417:   // structures. Then, they enter the second sync barrier. This\\n418:   // ensure, that no task starts doing work before all data\\n419:   // structures (local and global) have been re-initialized. When they\\n420:   // exit it, they are free to start working again.\\n421:   WorkerThreadsBarrierSync     _first_overflow_barrier_sync;\\n422:   WorkerThreadsBarrierSync     _second_overflow_barrier_sync;\\n423: \\n424:   // Number of completed mark cycles.\\n425:   volatile uint           _completed_mark_cycles;\\n426: \\n427:   // This is set by any task, when an overflow on the global data\\n428:   // structures is detected\\n429:   volatile bool           _has_overflown;\\n430:   // True: marking is concurrent, false: we're in remark\\n431:   volatile bool           _concurrent;\\n432:   // Set at the end of a Full GC so that marking aborts\\n433:   volatile bool           _has_aborted;\\n434: \\n435:   // Used when remark aborts due to an overflow to indicate that\\n436:   // another concurrent marking phase should start\\n437:   volatile bool           _restart_for_overflow;\\n438: \\n439:   ConcurrentGCTimer*      _gc_timer_cm;\\n440: \\n441:   G1OldTracer*            _gc_tracer_cm;\\n442: \\n443:   // Timing statistics. All of them are in ms\\n444:   NumberSeq _remark_times;\\n445:   NumberSeq _remark_mark_times;\\n446:   NumberSeq _remark_weak_ref_times;\\n447:   NumberSeq _cleanup_times;\\n448: \\n449:   double*   _accum_task_vtime;   // Accumulated task vtime\\n450: \\n451:   WorkerThreads* _concurrent_workers;\\n452:   uint      _num_concurrent_workers; // The number of marking worker threads we're using\\n453:   uint      _max_concurrent_workers; // Maximum number of marking worker threads\\n454: \\n455:   enum class VerifyLocation {\\n456:     RemarkBefore,\\n457:     RemarkAfter,\\n458:     RemarkOverflow,\\n459:     CleanupBefore,\\n460:     CleanupAfter\\n461:   };\\n462:   static const char* verify_location_string(VerifyLocation location);\\n463:   void verify_during_pause(G1HeapVerifier::G1VerifyType type,\\n464:                            VerifyLocation location);\\n465: \\n466:   void finalize_marking();\\n467: \\n468:   void weak_refs_work();\\n469: \\n470:   // After reclaiming empty regions, update heap sizes.\\n471:   void compute_new_sizes();\\n472: \\n473:   // Resets all the marking data structures. Called when we have to restart\\n474:   // marking or when marking completes (via set_non_marking_state below).\\n475:   void reset_marking_for_restart();\\n476: \\n477:   // We do this after we're done with marking so that the marking data\\n478:   // structures are initialized to a sensible and predictable state.\\n479:   void reset_at_marking_complete();\\n480: \\n481:   // Called to indicate how many threads are currently active.\\n482:   void set_concurrency(uint active_tasks);\\n483: \\n484:   // Should be called to indicate which phase we're in (concurrent\\n485:   // mark or remark) and how many threads are currently active.\\n486:   void set_concurrency_and_phase(uint active_tasks, bool concurrent);\\n487: \\n488:   // Prints all gathered CM-related statistics\\n489:   void print_stats();\\n490: \\n491:   HeapWord*           finger()       { return _finger;   }\\n492:   bool                concurrent()   { return _concurrent; }\\n493:   uint                active_tasks() { return _num_active_tasks; }\\n494:   TaskTerminator*     terminator()   { return &_terminator; }\\n495: \\n496:   // Claims the next available region to be scanned by a marking\\n497:   // task/thread. It might return null if the next region is empty or\\n498:   // we have run out of regions. In the latter case, out_of_regions()\\n499:   // determines whether we've really run out of regions or the task\\n500:   // should call claim_region() again. This might seem a bit\\n501:   // awkward. Originally, the code was written so that claim_region()\\n502:   // either successfully returned with a non-empty region or there\\n503:   // were no more regions to be claimed. The problem with this was\\n504:   // that, in certain circumstances, it iterated over large chunks of\\n505:   // the heap finding only empty regions and, while it was working, it\\n506:   // was preventing the calling task to call its regular clock\\n507:   // method. So, this way, each task will spend very little time in\\n508:   // claim_region() and is allowed to call the regular clock method\\n509:   // frequently.\\n510:   G1HeapRegion* claim_region(uint worker_id);\\n511: \\n512:   // Determines whether we've run out of regions to scan. Note that\\n513:   // the finger can point past the heap end in case the heap was expanded\\n514:   // to satisfy an allocation without doing a GC. This is fine, because all\\n515:   // objects in those regions will be considered live anyway because of\\n516:   // SATB guarantees (i.e. their TAMS will be equal to bottom).\\n517:   bool out_of_regions() { return _finger >= _heap.end(); }\\n518: \\n519:   // Returns the task with the given id\\n520:   G1CMTask* task(uint id) {\\n521:     // During concurrent start we use the parallel gc threads to do some work, so\\n522:     // we can only compare against _max_num_tasks.\\n523:     assert(id < _max_num_tasks, \\\"Task id %u not within bounds up to %u\\\", id, _max_num_tasks);\\n524:     return _tasks[id];\\n525:   }\\n526: \\n527:   // Access / manipulation of the overflow flag which is set to\\n528:   // indicate that the global stack has overflown\\n529:   bool has_overflown()           { return _has_overflown; }\\n530:   void set_has_overflown()       { _has_overflown = true; }\\n531:   void clear_has_overflown()     { _has_overflown = false; }\\n532:   bool restart_for_overflow()    { return _restart_for_overflow; }\\n533: \\n534:   // Methods to enter the two overflow sync barriers\\n535:   void enter_first_sync_barrier(uint worker_id);\\n536:   void enter_second_sync_barrier(uint worker_id);\\n537: \\n538:   // Clear the next marking bitmap in parallel using the given WorkerThreads. If may_yield is\\n539:   // true, periodically insert checks to see if this method should exit prematurely.\\n540:   void clear_bitmap(WorkerThreads* workers, bool may_yield);\\n541: \\n542:   // Region statistics gathered during marking.\\n543:   G1RegionMarkStats* _region_mark_stats;\\n544:   // Top pointer for each region at the start of marking. Must be valid for all committed\\n545:   // regions.\\n546:   HeapWord* volatile* _top_at_mark_starts;\\n547:   // Top pointer for each region at the start of the rebuild remembered set process\\n548:   // for regions which remembered sets need to be rebuilt. Both are pushed onto the mark stack.\\n56: class G1TaskQueueEntry {\\n57: private:\\n58:   void* _holder;\\n59: \\n60:   static const uintptr_t ArraySliceBit = 1;\\n61: \\n62:   G1TaskQueueEntry(oop obj) : _holder(obj) {\\n63:     assert(_holder != nullptr, \\\"Not allowed to set null task queue element\\\");\\n64:   }\\n65:   G1TaskQueueEntry(HeapWord* addr) : _holder((void*)((uintptr_t)addr | ArraySliceBit)) { }\\n66: public:\\n67: \\n68:   G1TaskQueueEntry() : _holder(nullptr) { }\\n69:   // Trivially copyable, for use in GenericTaskQueue.\\n70: \\n71:   static G1TaskQueueEntry from_slice(HeapWord* what) { return G1TaskQueueEntry(what); }\\n72:   static G1TaskQueueEntry from_oop(oop obj) { return G1TaskQueueEntry(obj); }\\n73: \\n74:   oop obj() const {\\n75:     assert(!is_array_slice(), \\\"Trying to read array slice \\\" PTR_FORMAT \\\" as oop\\\", p2i(_holder));\\n76:     return cast_to_oop(_holder);\\n77:   }\\n78: \\n79:   HeapWord* slice() const {\\n80:     assert(is_array_slice(), \\\"Trying to read oop \\\" PTR_FORMAT \\\" as array slice\\\", p2i(_holder));\\n81:     return (HeapWord*)((uintptr_t)_holder & ~ArraySliceBit);\\n82:   }\\n83: \\n84:   bool is_oop() const { return !is_array_slice(); }\\n85:   bool is_array_slice() const { return ((uintptr_t)_holder & ArraySliceBit) != 0; }\\n86:   bool is_null() const { return _holder == nullptr; }\\n87: };\\n88: \\n89: typedef GenericTaskQueue<G1TaskQueueEntry, mtGC> G1CMTaskQueue;\\n90: typedef GenericTaskQueueSet<G1CMTaskQueue, mtGC> G1CMTaskQueueSet;\\n91: \\n92: // Closure used by CM during concurrent reference discovery\\n93: // and reference processing (during remarking) to determine\\n94: // if a particular object is alive. It is primarily used\\n95: // to determine if referents of discovered reference objects\\n96: // are alive. An instance is also embedded into the\\n97: // reference processor as the _is_alive_non_header field\\n98: class G1CMIsAliveClosure : public BoolObjectClosure {\\n99:   G1ConcurrentMark* _cm;\\n100: \\n101: public:\\n102:   G1CMIsAliveClosure();\\n103:   G1CMIsAliveClosure(G1ConcurrentMark* cm);\\n104:   void initialize(G1ConcurrentMark* cm);\\n105: \\n106:   bool do_object_b(oop obj);\\n107: };\\n108: \\n109: class G1CMSubjectToDiscoveryClosure : public BoolObjectClosure {\\n110:   G1CollectedHeap* _g1h;\\n111: public:\\n112:   G1CMSubjectToDiscoveryClosure(G1CollectedHeap* g1h) : _g1h(g1h) { }\\n113:   bool do_object_b(oop obj);\\n114: };\\n115: \\n116: // Represents the overflow mark stack used by concurrent marking.\\n117: //\\n118: // Stores oops in a huge buffer in virtual memory that is always fully committed.\\n119: // Resizing may only happen during a STW pause when the stack is empty.\\n120: //\\n121: // Memory is allocated on a \\\"chunk\\\" basis, i.e. a set of oops. For this, the mark\\n122: // stack memory is split into evenly sized chunks of oops. Users can only\\n123: // add or remove entries on that basis.\\n124: // Chunks are filled in increasing address order. Not completely filled chunks\\n125: // have a null element as a terminating element.\\n126: //\\n127: // Every chunk has a header containing a single pointer element used for memory\\n128: // management. This wastes some space, but is negligible (< .1% with current sizing).\\n129: //\\n130: // Memory management is done using a mix of tracking a high water-mark indicating\\n131: // that all chunks at a lower address are valid chunks, and a singly linked free\\n132: // list connecting all empty chunks.\\n133: class G1CMMarkStack {\\n134: public:\\n135:   // Number of TaskQueueEntries that can fit in a single chunk.\\n136:   static const size_t EntriesPerChunk = 1024 - 1 /* One reference for the next pointer */;\\n137: private:\\n138:   struct TaskQueueEntryChunk {\\n139:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* next;\\n140:     G1TaskQueueEntry data[EntriesPerChunk];\\n141:   };\\n142: \\n143:   class ChunkAllocator {\\n144:     // The chunk allocator relies on a growable array data structure that allows resizing without the\\n145:     // need to copy existing items. The basic approach involves organizing the array into chunks,\\n146:     // essentially creating an \\\"array of arrays\\\"; referred to as buckets in this implementation. To\\n147:     // facilitate efficient indexing, the size of the first bucket is set to a power of 2. This choice\\n148:     // allows for quick conversion of an array index into a bucket index and the corresponding offset\\n149:     // within the bucket. Additionally, each new bucket added to the growable array doubles the capacity of\\n150:     // the growable array.\\n151:     //\\n152:     // Illustration of the growable array data structure.\\n153:     //\\n154:     //        +----+        +----+----+\\n155:     //        |    |------->|    |    |\\n156:     //        |    |        +----+----+\\n157:     //        +----+        +----+----+\\n158:     //        |    |------->|    |    |\\n159:     //        |    |        +----+----+\\n160:     //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\\n161:     //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |\\n162:     //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\\n163:     //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\\n164:     //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |     |     |     |    |\\n165:     //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\\n166:     //        +----+\\n167:     //\\n168:     size_t _min_capacity;\\n169:     size_t _max_capacity;\\n170:     size_t _capacity;\\n171:     size_t _num_buckets;\\n172:     bool _should_grow;\\n173:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* _buckets;\\n174:     char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\\n175:     volatile size_t _size;\\n176:     char _pad4[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(size_t)];\\n177: \\n178:     size_t bucket_size(size_t bucket) {\\n179:       return (bucket == 0) ?\\n180:               _min_capacity :\\n181:               _min_capacity * ( 1ULL << (bucket - 1));\\n182:     }\\n183: \\n184:     static unsigned int find_highest_bit(uintptr_t mask) {\\n185:       return count_leading_zeros(mask) ^ (BitsPerWord - 1U);\\n186:     }\\n187: \\n188:     size_t get_bucket(size_t array_idx) {\\n189:       if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\\n190:         return 0;\\n191:       }\\n192: \\n193:       return find_highest_bit(array_idx) - find_highest_bit(_min_capacity) + 1;\\n194:     }\\n195: \\n196:     size_t get_bucket_index(size_t array_idx) {\\n197:       if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\\n198:         return array_idx;\\n199:       }\\n200:       return array_idx - (1ULL << find_highest_bit(array_idx));\\n201:     }\\n202: \\n203:     bool reserve(size_t new_capacity);\\n204: \\n205:   public:\\n206:     ChunkAllocator();\\n207: \\n208:     ~ChunkAllocator();\\n209: \\n210:     bool initialize(size_t initial_capacity, size_t max_capacity);\\n211: \\n212:     void reset() {\\n213:       _size = 0;\\n214:       _should_grow = false;\\n215:     }\\n216: \\n217:     // During G1CMConcurrentMarkingTask or finalize_marking phases, we prefer to restart the marking when\\n218:     // the G1CMMarkStack overflows. Attempts to expand the G1CMMarkStack should be followed with a restart\\n219:     // of the marking. On failure to allocate a new chuck, the caller just returns and forces a restart.\\n220:     // This approach offers better memory utilization for the G1CMMarkStack, as each iteration of the\\n221:     // marking potentially involves traversing fewer unmarked nodes in the graph.\\n222: \\n223:     // However, during the reference processing phase, instead of restarting the marking process, the\\n224:     // G1CMMarkStack is expanded upon failure to allocate a new chunk. The decision between these two\\n225:     // modes of expansion is determined by the _should_grow parameter.\\n226:     void set_should_grow() {\\n227:       _should_grow = true;\\n228:     }\\n229: \\n230:     size_t capacity() const { return _capacity; }\\n231: \\n232:     // Expand the mark stack doubling its size.\\n233:     bool try_expand();\\n234:     bool try_expand_to(size_t desired_capacity);\\n235: \\n236:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* allocate_new_chunk();\\n237:   };\\n238: \\n239:   ChunkAllocator _chunk_allocator;\\n240: \\n241:   char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\\n242:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _free_list;  // Linked list of free chunks that can be allocated by users.\\n243:   char _pad1[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*)];\\n244:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _chunk_list; // List of chunks currently containing data.\\n245:   volatile size_t _chunks_in_chunk_list;\\n246:   char _pad2[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*) - sizeof(size_t)];\\n247: \\n248:   // Atomically add the given chunk to the list.\\n249:   void add_chunk_to_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* list, TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\\n250:   // Atomically remove and return a chunk from the given list. Returns null if the\\n251:   // list is empty.\\n252:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* list);\\n253: \\n254:   void add_chunk_to_chunk_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\\n255:   void add_chunk_to_free_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\\n256: \\n257:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_chunk_list();\\n258:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* remove_chunk_from_free_list();\\n259: \\n260:  public:\\n261:   G1CMMarkStack();\\n262:   ~G1CMMarkStack() = default;\\n263: \\n264:   // Alignment and minimum capacity of this mark stack in number of oops.\\n265:   static size_t capacity_alignment();\\n266: \\n267:   // Allocate and initialize the mark stack.\\n268:   bool initialize();\\n269: \\n270:   // Pushes the given buffer containing at most EntriesPerChunk elements on the mark\\n271:   // stack. If less than EntriesPerChunk elements are to be pushed, the array must\\n272:   // be terminated with a null.\\n273:   // Returns whether the buffer contents were successfully pushed to the global mark\\n274:   // stack.\\n275:   bool par_push_chunk(G1TaskQueueEntry* buffer);\\n276: \\n277:   // Pops a chunk from this mark stack, copying them into the given buffer. This\\n278:   // chunk may contain up to EntriesPerChunk elements. If there are less, the last\\n279:   // element in the array is a null pointer.\\n280:   bool par_pop_chunk(G1TaskQueueEntry* buffer);\\n281: \\n282:   // Return whether the chunk list is empty. Racy due to unsynchronized access to\\n283:   // _chunk_list.\\n284:   bool is_empty() const { return _chunk_list == nullptr; }\\n285: \\n286:   size_t capacity() const  { return _chunk_allocator.capacity(); }\\n287: \\n288:   void set_should_grow() {\\n289:     _chunk_allocator.set_should_grow();\\n290:   }\\n291: \\n292:   // Expand the stack, typically in response to an overflow condition\\n293:   void expand();\\n294: \\n295:   // Return the approximate number of oops on this mark stack. Racy due to\\n296:   // unsynchronized access to _chunks_in_chunk_list.\\n297:   size_t size() const { return _chunks_in_chunk_list * EntriesPerChunk; }\\n298: \\n299:   void set_empty();\\n300: \\n301:   // Apply Fn to every oop on the mark stack. The mark stack must not\\n302:   // be modified while iterating.\\n303:   template<typename Fn> void iterate(Fn fn) const PRODUCT_RETURN;\\n304: };\\n305: \\n306: // Root MemRegions are memory areas that contain objects which references are\\n307: // roots wrt to the marking. They must be scanned before marking to maintain the\\n308: // SATB invariant.\\n309: // Typically they contain the areas from TAMS to top of the regions.\\n310: // We could scan and mark through these objects during the concurrent start pause,\\n311: // but for pause time reasons we move this work to the concurrent phase.\\n312: // We need to complete this procedure before we can evacuate a particular region\\n313: // because evacuation might determine that some of these \\\"root objects\\\" are dead,\\n314: // potentially dropping some required references.\\n315: // Root MemRegions comprise of the contents of survivor regions at the end\\n316: // of the GC, and any objects copied into the old gen during GC.\\n317: class G1CMRootMemRegions {\\n318:   // The set of root MemRegions.\\n319:   MemRegion* _root_regions;\\n320:   size_t const _max_regions;\\n321: \\n322:   volatile size_t _num_root_regions; // Actual number of root regions.\\n323: \\n324:   volatile size_t _claimed_root_regions; // Number of root regions currently claimed.\\n325: \\n326:   volatile bool _scan_in_progress;\\n327:   volatile bool _should_abort;\\n328: \\n329:   void notify_scan_done();\\n330: \\n331: public:\\n332:   G1CMRootMemRegions(uint const max_regions);\\n333:   ~G1CMRootMemRegions();\\n334: \\n335:   // Reset the data structure to allow addition of new root regions.\\n336:   void reset();\\n337: \\n338:   void add(HeapWord* start, HeapWord* end);\\n339: \\n340:   // Reset the claiming / scanning of the root regions.\\n341:   void prepare_for_scan();\\n342: \\n343:   // Forces get_next() to return null so that the iteration aborts early.\\n344:   void abort() { _should_abort = true; }\\n345: \\n346:   // Return true if the CM thread are actively scanning root regions,\\n347:   // false otherwise.\\n348:   bool scan_in_progress() { return _scan_in_progress; }\\n349: \\n350:   // Claim the next root MemRegion to scan atomically, or return null if\\n351:   // all have been claimed.\\n352:   const MemRegion* claim_next();\\n353: \\n354:   // The number of root regions to scan.\\n355:   uint num_root_regions() const;\\n356: \\n357:   // Is the given memregion contained in the root regions; the MemRegion must\\n358:   // match exactly.\\n359:   bool contains(const MemRegion mr) const;\\n360: \\n361:   void cancel_scan();\\n362: \\n363:   // Flag that we're done with root region scanning and notify anyone\\n364:   // who's waiting on it. If aborted is false, assume that all regions\\n365:   // have been claimed.\\n366:   void scan_finished();\\n367: \\n368:   // If CM threads are still scanning root regions, wait until they\\n369:   // are done. Return true if we had to wait, false otherwise.\\n370:   bool wait_until_scan_finished();\\n371: };\\n372: \\n373: // This class manages data structures and methods for doing liveness analysis in\\n374: // G1's concurrent cycle.\\n375: class G1ConcurrentMark : public CHeapObj<mtGC> {\\n376:   friend class G1CMBitMapClosure;\\n377:   friend class G1CMConcurrentMarkingTask;\\n378:   friend class G1CMDrainMarkingStackClosure;\\n379:   friend class G1CMKeepAliveAndDrainClosure;\\n380:   friend class G1CMRefProcProxyTask;\\n381:   friend class G1CMRemarkTask;\\n382:   friend class G1CMRootRegionScanTask;\\n383:   friend class G1CMTask;\\n384:   friend class G1ConcurrentMarkThread;\\n385: \\n386:   G1ConcurrentMarkThread* _cm_thread;     // The thread doing the work\\n387:   G1CollectedHeap*        _g1h;           // The heap\\n388: \\n389:   // Concurrent marking support structures\\n390:   G1CMBitMap              _mark_bitmap;\\n391: \\n392:   // Heap bounds\\n393:   MemRegion const         _heap;\\n394: \\n395:   // Root region tracking and claiming\\n396:   G1CMRootMemRegions      _root_regions;\\n397: \\n398:   // For grey objects\\n399:   G1CMMarkStack           _global_mark_stack; // Grey objects behind global finger\\n400:   HeapWord* volatile      _finger;            // The global finger, region aligned,\\n401:                                               // always pointing to the end of the\\n402:                                               // last claimed region\\n403: \\n404:   uint                    _worker_id_offset;\\n405:   uint                    _max_num_tasks;    // Maximum number of marking tasks\\n406:   uint                    _num_active_tasks; // Number of tasks currently active\\n407:   G1CMTask**              _tasks;            // Task queue array (max_worker_id length)\\n408: \\n409:   G1CMTaskQueueSet*       _task_queues; // Task queue set\\n410:   TaskTerminator          _terminator;  // For termination\\n411: \\n412:   // Two sync barriers that are used to synchronize tasks when an\\n413:   // overflow occurs. The algorithm is the following. All tasks enter\\n414:   // the first one to ensure that they have all stopped manipulating\\n415:   // the global data structures. After they exit it, they re-initialize\\n416:   // their data structures and task 0 re-initializes the global data\\n417:   // structures. Then, they enter the second sync barrier. This\\n418:   // ensure, that no task starts doing work before all data\\n419:   // structures (local and global) have been re-initialized. When they\\n420:   // exit it, they are free to start working again.\\n421:   WorkerThreadsBarrierSync     _first_overflow_barrier_sync;\\n422:   WorkerThreadsBarrierSync     _second_overflow_barrier_sync;\\n423: \\n424:   // Number of completed mark cycles.\\n425:   volatile uint           _completed_mark_cycles;\\n426: \\n427:   // This is set by any task, when an overflow on the global data\\n428:   // structures is detected\\n429:   volatile bool           _has_overflown;\\n430:   // True: marking is concurrent, false: we're in remark\\n431:   volatile bool           _concurrent;\\n432:   // Set at the end of a Full GC so that marking aborts\\n433:   volatile bool           _has_aborted;\\n434: \\n435:   // Used when remark aborts due to an overflow to indicate that\\n436:   // another concurrent marking phase should start\\n437:   volatile bool           _restart_for_overflow;\\n438: \\n439:   ConcurrentGCTimer*      _gc_timer_cm;\\n440: \\n441:   G1OldTracer*            _gc_tracer_cm;\\n442: \\n443:   // Timing statistics. All of them are in ms\\n444:   NumberSeq _remark_times;\\n445:   NumberSeq _remark_mark_times;\\n446:   NumberSeq _remark_weak_ref_times;\\n447:   NumberSeq _cleanup_times;\\n448: \\n449:   double*   _accum_task_vtime;   // Accumulated task vtime\\n450: \\n451:   WorkerThreads* _concurrent_workers;\\n452:   uint      _num_concurrent_workers; // The number of marking worker threads we're using\\n453:   uint      _max_concurrent_workers; // Maximum number of marking worker threads\\n454: \\n455:   enum class VerifyLocation {\\n456:     RemarkBefore,\\n457:     RemarkAfter,\\n458:     RemarkOverflow,\\n459:     CleanupBefore,\\n460:     CleanupAfter\\n461:   };\\n462:   static const char* verify_location_string(VerifyLocation location);\\n463:   void verify_during_pause(G1HeapVerifier::G1VerifyType type,\\n464:                            VerifyLocation location);\\n465: \\n466:   void finalize_marking();\\n467: \\n468:   void weak_refs_work();\\n469: \\n470:   // After reclaiming empty regions, update heap sizes.\\n471:   void compute_new_sizes();\\n472: \\n473:   // Resets all the marking data structures. Called when we have to restart\\n474:   // marking or when marking completes (via set_non_marking_state below).\\n475:   void reset_marking_for_restart();\\n476: \\n477:   // We do this after we're done with marking so that the marking data\\n478:   // structures are initialized to a sensible and predictable state.\\n479:   void reset_at_marking_complete();\\n480: \\n481:   // Called to indicate how many threads are currently active.\\n482:   void set_concurrency(uint active_tasks);\\n483: \\n484:   // Should be called to indicate which phase we're in (concurrent\\n485:   // mark or remark) and how many threads are currently active.\\n486:   void set_concurrency_and_phase(uint active_tasks, bool concurrent);\\n487: \\n488:   // Prints all gathered CM-related statistics\\n489:   void print_stats();\\n490: \\n491:   HeapWord*           finger()       { return _finger;   }\\n492:   bool                concurrent()   { return _concurrent; }\\n493:   uint                active_tasks() { return _num_active_tasks; }\\n494:   TaskTerminator*     terminator()   { return &_terminator; }\\n495: \\n496:   // Claims the next available region to be scanned by a marking\\n497:   // task/thread. It might return null if the next region is empty or\\n498:   // we have run out of regions. In the latter case, out_of_regions()\\n499:   // determines whether we've really run out of regions or the task\\n500:   // should call claim_region() again. This might seem a bit\\n501:   // awkward. Originally, the code was written so that claim_region()\\n502:   // either successfully returned with a non-empty region or there\\n503:   // were no more regions to be claimed. The problem with this was\\n504:   // that, in certain circumstances, it iterated over large chunks of\\n505:   // the heap finding only empty regions and, while it was working, it\\n506:   // was preventing the calling task to call its regular clock\\n507:   // method. So, this way, each task will spend very little time in\\n508:   // claim_region() and is allowed to call the regular clock method\\n509:   // frequently.\\n510:   G1HeapRegion* claim_region(uint worker_id);\\n511: \\n512:   // Determines whether we've run out of regions to scan. Note that\\n513:   // the finger can point past the heap end in case the heap was expanded\\n514:   // to satisfy an allocation without doing a GC. This is fine, because all\\n515:   // objects in those regions will be considered live anyway because of\\n516:   // SATB guarantees (i.e. their TAMS will be equal to bottom).\\n517:   bool out_of_regions() { return _finger >= _heap.end(); }\\n518: \\n519:   // Returns the task with the given id\\n520:   G1CMTask* task(uint id) {\\n521:     // During concurrent start we use the parallel gc threads to do some work, so\\n522:     // we can only compare against _max_num_tasks.\\n523:     assert(id < _max_num_tasks, \\\"Task id %u not within bounds up to %u\\\", id, _max_num_tasks);\\n524:     return _tasks[id];\\n525:   }\\n526: \\n527:   // Access / manipulation of the overflow flag which is set to\\n528:   // indicate that the global stack has overflown\\n529:   bool has_overflown()           { return _has_overflown; }\\n530:   void set_has_overflown()       { _has_overflown = true; }\\n531:   void clear_has_overflown()     { _has_overflown = false; }\\n532:   bool restart_for_overflow()    { return _restart_for_overflow; }\\n533: \\n534:   // Methods to enter the two overflow sync barriers\\n535:   void enter_first_sync_barrier(uint worker_id);\\n536:   void enter_second_sync_barrier(uint worker_id);\\n537: \\n538:   // Clear the next marking bitmap in parallel using the given WorkerThreads. If may_yield is\\n539:   // true, periodically insert checks to see if this method should exit prematurely.\\n540:   void clear_bitmap(WorkerThreads* workers, bool may_yield);\\n541: \\n542:   // Region statistics gathered during marking.\\n543:   G1RegionMarkStats* _region_mark_stats;\\n544:   // Top pointer for each region at the start of marking. Must be valid for all committed\\n545:   // regions.\\n546:   HeapWord* volatile* _top_at_mark_starts;\\n547:   // Top pointer for each region at the start of the rebuild remembered set process\\n548:   // for regions which remembered sets need to be rebuilt. For this, the mark\n122: // stack memory is split into evenly sized chunks of oops. Users can only\n123: // add or remove entries on that basis.\n124: // Chunks are filled in increasing address order. Not completely filled chunks\n125: // have a null element as a terminating element.\n126: //\n127: // Every chunk has a header containing a single pointer element used for memory\n128: // management. This wastes some space, but is negligible (< .1% with current sizing).\n129: //\n130: // Memory management is done using a mix of tracking a high water-mark indicating\n131: // that all chunks at a lower address are valid chunks, and a singly linked free\n132: // list connecting all empty chunks.\n133: class G1CMMarkStack {\n134: public:\n135:   // Number of TaskQueueEntries that can fit in a single chunk.\n136:   static const size_t EntriesPerChunk = 1024 - 1 /* One reference for the next pointer */;\n137: private:\n138:   struct TaskQueueEntryChunk {\n139:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* next;\n140:     G1TaskQueueEntry data[EntriesPerChunk];\n141:   };\n142: \n143:   class ChunkAllocator {\n144:     // The chunk allocator relies on a growable array data structure that allows resizing without the\n145:     // need to copy existing items. The basic approach involves organizing the array into chunks,\n146:     // essentially creating an \"array of arrays\"; referred to as buckets in this implementation. To\n147:     // facilitate efficient indexing, the size of the first bucket is set to a power of 2. This choice\n148:     // allows for quick conversion of an array index into a bucket index and the corresponding offset\n149:     // within the bucket. Additionally, each new bucket added to the growable array doubles the capacity of\n150:     // the growable array.\n151:     //\n152:     // Illustration of the growable array data structure.\n153:     //\n154:     //        +----+        +----+----+\n155:     //        |    |------->|    |    |\n156:     //        |    |        +----+----+\n157:     //        +----+        +----+----+\n158:     //        |    |------->|    |    |\n159:     //        |    |        +----+----+\n160:     //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\n161:     //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |\n162:     //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+\n163:     //        +----+        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\n164:     //        |    |------->|     |     |     |     |     |     |     |    |\n165:     //        |    |        +-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+-----+----+\n166:     //        +----+\n167:     //\n168:     size_t _min_capacity;\n169:     size_t _max_capacity;\n170:     size_t _capacity;\n171:     size_t _num_buckets;\n172:     bool _should_grow;\n173:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* _buckets;\n174:     char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\n175:     volatile size_t _size;\n176:     char _pad4[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(size_t)];\n177: \n178:     size_t bucket_size(size_t bucket) {\n179:       return (bucket == 0) ?\n180:               _min_capacity :\n181:               _min_capacity * ( 1ULL << (bucket - 1));\n182:     }\n183: \n184:     static unsigned int find_highest_bit(uintptr_t mask) {\n185:       return count_leading_zeros(mask) ^ (BitsPerWord - 1U);\n186:     }\n187: \n188:     size_t get_bucket(size_t array_idx) {\n189:       if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\n190:         return 0;\n191:       }\n192: \n193:       return find_highest_bit(array_idx) - find_highest_bit(_min_capacity) + 1;\n194:     }\n195: \n196:     size_t get_bucket_index(size_t array_idx) {\n197:       if (array_idx < _min_capacity) {\n198:         return array_idx;\n199:       }\n200:       return array_idx - (1ULL << find_highest_bit(array_idx));\n201:     }\n202: \n203:     bool reserve(size_t new_capacity);\n204: \n205:   public:\n206:     ChunkAllocator();\n207: \n208:     ~ChunkAllocator();\n209: \n210:     bool initialize(size_t initial_capacity, size_t max_capacity);\n211: \n212:     void reset() {\n213:       _size = 0;\n214:       _should_grow = false;\n215:     }\n216: \n217:     // During G1CMConcurrentMarkingTask or finalize_marking phases, we prefer to restart the marking when\n218:     // the G1CMMarkStack overflows. Attempts to expand the G1CMMarkStack should be followed with a restart\n219:     // of the marking. On failure to allocate a new chuck, the caller just returns and forces a restart.\n220:     // This approach offers better memory utilization for the G1CMMarkStack, as each iteration of the\n221:     // marking potentially involves traversing fewer unmarked nodes in the graph.\n222: \n223:     // However, during the reference processing phase, instead of restarting the marking process, the\n224:     // G1CMMarkStack is expanded upon failure to allocate a new chunk. The decision between these two\n225:     // modes of expansion is determined by the _should_grow parameter.\n226:     void set_should_grow() {\n227:       _should_grow = true;\n228:     }\n229: \n230:     size_t capacity() const { return _capacity; }\n231: \n232:     // Expand the mark stack doubling its size.\n233:     bool try_expand();\n234:     bool try_expand_to(size_t desired_capacity);\n235: \n236:     TaskQueueEntryChunk* allocate_new_chunk();\n237:   };\n238: \n239:   ChunkAllocator _chunk_allocator;\n240: \n241:   char _pad0[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE];\n242:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _free_list;  // Linked list of free chunks that can be allocated by users.\n243:   char _pad1[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*)];\n244:   TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile _chunk_list; // List of chunks currently containing data.\n245:   volatile size_t _chunks_in_chunk_list;\n246:   char _pad2[DEFAULT_PADDING_SIZE - sizeof(TaskQueueEntryChunk*) - sizeof(size_t)];\n247: \n248:   // Atomically add the given chunk to the list.\n249:   void add_chunk_to_list(TaskQueueEntryChunk* volatile* list, TaskQueueEntryChunk* elem);\n250:   // Atomically remove and return a chunk from the given list. // Task queue set\n410:   TaskTerminator          _terminator;  // For termination\n411: \n412:   // Two sync barriers that are used to synchronize tasks when an\n413:   // overflow occurs. In particular, it must not\\n52: // be a null pointer.  null pointers are pre-filtered and never\\n53: // inserted into a SATB buffer.\\n54: //\\n55: // An entry that is below the TAMS pointer for the containing heap\\n56: // region requires marking. Such an entry must point to a valid object.\\n57: //\\n58: // An entry that is at least the TAMS pointer for the containing heap\\n59: // region might be any of the following, none of which should be marked.\\n60: //\\n61: // * A reference to an object allocated since marking started.\\n62: //   According to SATB, such objects are implicitly kept live and do\\n63: //   not need to be dealt with via SATB buffer processing.\\n64: //\\n65: // * A reference to a young generation object. Young objects are\\n66: //   handled separately and are not marked by concurrent marking.\\n67: //\\n68: // * A stale reference to a young generation object. If a young\\n69: //   generation object reference is recorded and not filtered out\\n70: //   before being moved by a young collection, the reference becomes\\n71: //   stale.\\n72: //\\n73: // * A stale reference to an eagerly reclaimed humongous object.  If a\\n74: //   humongous object is recorded and then reclaimed, the reference\\n75: //   becomes stale.\\n76: //\\n77: // The stale reference cases are implicitly handled by the TAMS\\n78: // comparison. collector's concurrent marking and mixed collection cycle is orchestrated through a complex chain of C++ components in openjdk/jdk. Here's how the major phases are implemented:\\n\\n### 1. Concurrent Mark Cycle Start Trigger\\n\\nThe concurrent marking cycle is initiated through the following call chain:\\n- **G1ConcurrentMarkThread::concurrent_cycle_start()** (g1ConcurrentMarkThread.cpp:267) calls\\n- **G1ConcurrentMark::concurrent_cycle_start()** (g1ConcurrentMark.cpp:1114) which registers the GC start time\\n\\nFollowed by:\\n- **G1ConcurrentMark::post_concurrent_mark_start()** (g1ConcurrentMark.cpp:908) which:\\n  - Starts concurrent marking weak-reference discovery via the reference processor\\n  - Activates SATB queues for all threads via **G1BarrierSet::satb_mark_queue_set()**\\n  - Prepares root regions for scanning\\n\\n### 2. SATB Marking Queue Processing\\n\\nThe Snapshot-At-The-Beginning (SATB) invariant is maintained through:\\n\\n**G1CMTask::drain_satb_buffers()** (g1ConcurrentMark.cpp:2424) which:\\n- Processes SATB buffers during concurrent marking using **G1CMSATBBufferClosure**\\n- Applies the closure to completed buffers via **SATBMarkQueueSet::apply_closure_to_completed_buffer()**\\n- Marks objects that require processing before they can be reclaimed\\n\\n**G1SATBMarkQueueSet::filter()** (g1SATBMarkQueueSet.cpp:116) which:\\n- Filters entries using **G1SATBMarkQueueFilterFn** closure\\n- Discards entries below TAMS (Top At Mark Start) that were allocated after marking started\\n- Removes entries for objects that are already marked using **G1CMBitMap**\\n\\nThe filtering logic in **requires_marking()** (g1SATBMarkQueueSet.cpp:82) ensures that only objects allocated before or at mark start time are processed.\\n\\n### 3.
